## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (mechanical vibrations / nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The variables x (position), v (velocity), t (time), and dv_dt (acceleration) match a second-order oscillator written as a first-order system, where dv_dt is typically a restoring force term in x plus damping terms in v and possibly explicit time-dependent forcing/parametric excitation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (linear restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small oscillations, conservative linear spring)
- Linear viscous damping added: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (damped linear oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (common nonlinear vibration model)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (stronger nonlinearity at large |x|)
- Pendulum-like restoring (geometric nonlinearity): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (large-angle oscillations approximation)
- Soft-saturation spring (bounded restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * tanh(c1 * x) - c2 * v (restoring force saturates for large |x|)
- Rational (softening) spring: dv_dt = -c0 * x / (c1 + x**2) - c2 * v (effective stiffness decreases with amplitude)
- Quadratic/drag-like damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (nonlinear dissipation at higher speeds)
- Dry (Coulomb) friction damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * sign(v) (stick-slip/constant friction magnitude)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited damping): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (negative damping at small |x|, limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent self-excitation): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (limit-cycle model in aero/structures)
- Externally forced oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (harmonic forcing in time)
- Forced Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (bistability/jump phenomena)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * x - c4 * v (Mathieu-type stiffness modulation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring forces are typically odd in x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x**3, -c*sin(c*x)); this symmetry implies dv_dt changes sign when x changes sign.
- Dissipation terms are typically odd in v (e.g., -c*v, -c*v*Abs(v), -c*sign(v)); these always oppose motion and reduce energy over time.
- Cubic stiffness (-c*x**3) produces amplitude-dependent frequency: positive coefficient tends to harden (frequency increases with amplitude), negative tends to soften.
- Bounded nonlinearities (tanh, sin) encode physical limits/geometry: restoring force grows slowly or is periodic in x, preventing unbounded acceleration at large |x|.
- Self-excited oscillations appear as damping that changes sign with state magnitude (e.g., (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v), yielding a stable limit cycle.
- Explicit periodic dependence on t (cos(c*t), sin(c*t)) indicates external forcing; it can create resonance, entrainment, and subharmonics.
- Multiplicative time dependence with x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) indicates parametric excitation, which can cause instability tongues (Mathieu behavior).
- Non-smooth terms in v (Abs(v), sign(v)) suggest impacts/frictional interfaces; they often generate harmonics and may require piecewise interpretations.
